Dear Ms Yanagawa
This report summarizes our geotechnical engineering observations and testing
services performed during construction of the Sea Country Area 7 Phase I and Phase II
project from May 27 2009 to in accordance with our fee proposals dated
May 15 2009 and for Phase I and Phase II respectively
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS
Sea Country is a residential subdivision development about 3 500 feet east of
Farrington Highway from its intersection with Kaukama Road in Waianae Oahu Hawaii
as shown on the Project Location Plan Plate 1 Sea Country is subdivided into several
project development areas one of these is Area 7 which is situated immediately north of
the existing Maili Kai Community Park including a row of 10 lots bordering the west side
of the park Area 7 is further subdivided into two phases namely Phase I and Phase II
Phase I encompasses an area of about 10 56 acres and constitutes the southern
half of Area 7 The development of Phase I includes the construction of 165 units of
single family residential lots designated as Lot Nos 1 through 102 104 through 116 and
118 through 167 Phase I also includes the construction of the subdivision road network
comprising of Roads A through G Road I and Pakeke Street Extension
D R Horton Schuler Division
Page 2
August 13 2013
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
Phase II constitutes the northern half of Area 7 and includes the development of
117 single family residential units designated as Lot Nos 1 through 91 and 93 through
118 The development also includes the extension of Roads B and C from Phase I
northwards into Phase II and the construction of two lateral roads namely Road H and
Road K as shown on the Overall General Plan Plate 2
Our monitoring services during construction consisted of moisture and density
testing to determine adequacy of compaction of fills and backfills for utility installations
pavement construction building pads garages walkways and driveways The
Site Grading Plans are shown on Plates 3 1 through 3 4
This report summarizes our field observations and compaction testing services for
the site grading operations and infrastructure installation for the Sea Country Area 7
Phase I and Phase II project
MASS GRADING
The mass grading for Phase I and Phase II of the Sea Country Area 7 project
consisted entirely of cuts and fills generally less than 5 feet on the naturally occurring
on site coralline materials to design grade It also involved the removal and replacement
of localized expansive alluvial surface deposits with non expansive coralline fill where
these were encountered Generally the upper 3 feet of fill at the site consisted primarily
of crushed coral materials
The fill and backfill materials were moisture conditioned to above optimum
moisture content and compacted to a minimum of 90 percent of the maximum dry
density as determined in accordance with ASTM D 1557 In the roadway areas the fill
and backfill materials within 2 feet of the finished subgrade were compacted to a
minimum of 95 percent relative density
SITE GRADING
The fine grading of the residential lot areas were concurrently completed during
the mass grading phase In conducting our construction monitoring services during
construction samples of the materials utilized as fill were obtained and transported to
our laboratory for testing The maximum dry densities and optimum moisture contents
were established in general accordance with ASTM D 1557 Modified Proctor A
summary of the test results are presented on Plates 4 1 through 4 4
Periodic field density tests were performed on prepared surfaces of controlled
fills and backfills in general accordance with ASTM D 6938 Nuclear Gauge Method
The test results are summarized on Plates 5 1 through 5 134 Test locations and
elevations were estimated using on site survey stakes for reference These locations
and elevations should be considered accurate only to the degree implied by the
methods used Areas assessed to be unsatisfactory were reworked until the measured
D R Horton Schuler Division
Page 3
August 13 2013
GEOLABS INC
Hawaii California
relative compaction conformed to or exceeded the minimum specified requirement for
the project
Our services consisted of full time and part time field observation of the
contractor s Delta Construction Corporation for Phase I and Royal Contracting for
Phase II subgrade preparation fill and backfill placement and compaction procedures
and confirmation of subgrade soil conditions exposed during the above site grading
operations
Based on our field representative s observations and the referenced test results
it is our opinion that the utility installation work and site grading for Phase I and Phase II
of the Sea Country Area 7 development project observed and tested by Geolabs in the
period covered by this report were performed in accordance with the general intent of
the recommendations in the following references
1
Chapter 14 of the Revised Ordinances of Honolulu 1990 as amended
2
Report by Geolabs Inc entitled Geotechnical Engineering Exploration
Sea Country Area 7 Maili Oahu Hawaii dated
HOUSE CONSTRUCTION CONSIDERATIONS
The finished grades adjacent to the structures should be sloped to shed water
away from the foundations and to reduce the potential for ponding It is also advised to
install gutter systems around the house structures to collect and discharge water away
from the foundation and pavement areas Excessive landscape watering within 3 feet of
the foundations and slabs should be avoided Gravel strips adjacent to slabs and
foundations should be avoided Planters next to foundations should be avoided or have
concrete bottoms and drains to reduce water infiltration into the subsoils
These drainage requirements are essential for the proper performance of the
building foundations since ponded water could cause subsurface soil saturation and
subsequent loss of strength of the near surface soils The foundation excavations
should be properly backfilled against the footings immediately after setting of the
concrete to reduce water infiltration Drainage swales should be provided as soon as
possible and should be maintained to drain surface run off away from foundations
Landscaping of the house lots by the homeowners is recommended to reduce the
potential for erosion and for altering the drainage patterns
D R Horton Schuler Division

LIMITATIONS
Geolabs assumes no responsibility for alterations made to finished grades on the
project subsequent to our observation and testing period without our knowledge and
written acknowledgment
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities
occurring simultaneously on a construction site therefore some work may have
occurred without our observation However we believe the level of earthwork
observation and testing services provided is reasonable in reducing the geotechnical
risks to the project It should be recognized that there are variations in the accuracy
and statistical repeatability of the tests and methods used to monitor the earthwork
construction and materials Our services were performed in accordance with generally
accepted standards of geotechnical engineering practice no warranty is expressed or
implied Provision of construction monitoring by an engineer is not insurance nor does
it guarantee construction of any type The contractor shall retain responsibility for the
quality of the work for adhering to the plans and specifications and for repairing defects
regardless of when they are found
